**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Architecture Map: Scientific Computing Data Flow

## Your Task

You are onboarding to a scientific computing team that uses the Python ML stack.
A senior engineer has asked you to produce a technical map of how data flows from
**raw array creation through scientific computation** across the three core libraries:
numpy, pandas, and scipy.

**Your question**: Map the data flow from raw array creation through scientific
computation across these repos. Your explanation must trace through all three layers:

1. **Array computation layer** — What function in `numpy/numpy` is the canonical
   entry point for array-level aggregation on raw ndarray objects?
2. **Data structure layer** — What class in `pandas-dev/pandas` wraps a NumPy ndarray
   as a pandas extension array, enabling interoperability between the two libraries?
3. **Scientific computation layer** — What function in `scipy/scipy` accepts numpy
   arrays (or pandas Series) as inputs for statistical analysis?

For each step, cite the specific repository, file path, and function/class name.

## Context

You are working with the Python ML stack in a cross-org environment:

- `scikit-learn/scikit-learn` (ML algorithms)
- `numpy/numpy` (array-computing)
- `pandas-dev/pandas` (dataframe-library)
- `scipy/scipy` (scientific-computing)

This question is specifically designed to benefit from cross-repo synthesis. The
data flow spans multiple organizations and can only be fully understood by examining
all three repos together.

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings:

```json
{
  "chain": [
    {
      "repo": "numpy/numpy",
      "path": "relative/path/to/file.py",
      "symbol": "FunctionOrClassName",
      "description": "What role this plays in the data flow"
    }
  ],
  "text": "Comprehensive narrative explaining how data flows from raw array creation through scientific computation, citing specific files and functions from each repo."
}
```

**Important**: Use exact repo identifiers as they appear in Sourcegraph. The oracle expects `repo` values of `numpy/numpy` (array layer), `pandas-dev/pandas` (data structure layer), and `scipy/scipy` (scientific computation layer). The `repo` field must match these exactly.
**Note**: Sourcegraph MCP tools return repo names with a `github.com/` prefix (e.g., `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go`). Strip this prefix in your answer — use `sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go`, NOT `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go`.
**Provenance**: Your `text` narrative is evaluated for completeness. It must include repository names verbatim in `org/repo` format (e.g., `numpy/numpy`, `pandas-dev/pandas`, `scipy/scipy`) and file paths using slash notation (e.g., `numpy/_core/fromnumeric.py`), not Python module dot notation.

The `chain` should contain at least 3 steps representing the 3 layers described above.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **Flow coverage**: Does the chain include key steps from all 3 layers (array creation → pandas integration → scipy computation)?
- **Technical accuracy**: Are the cited file paths and function/class names correct?
- **Provenance**: Does your narrative reference all three repositories with specific file paths?
- **Synthesis quality** (supplementary): Does the explanation connect the layers in a way that reveals the ecosystem architecture?

## Summary

I've mapped the data flow through three layers of the scientific Python stack:

1. **Array Computation Layer** (numpy/numpy): The `sum()` function in `numpy/_core/fromnumeric.py` serves as the canonical entry point for array-level aggregation on raw ndarray objects. It uses the `_wrapreduction()` mechanism to delegate to NumPy's universal functions.

2. **Data Structure Layer** (pandas-dev/pandas): The `NDArrayBackedExtensionArray` class in `pandas/core/arrays/_mixins.py` wraps a NumPy ndarray as a pandas extension array. It's the bridge that enables pandas DataFrames and Series to seamlessly work with NumPy's underlying arrays while providing labeled access and convenience methods.

3. **Scientific Computation Layer** (scipy/scipy): The `describe()` function in `scipy/stats/_stats_py.py` accepts array-like inputs (both raw NumPy arrays and pandas Series) and applies statistical transformations including mean, variance, skewness, and kurtosis calculations.

This function accepts array-like inputs and performs element-wise summation via the _wrapreduction() mechanism, which dispatches to the add universal function's reduce() method. The function supports axis selection, dtype specification, keepdims retention, and initial value control. This is the low-level primitive for all numerical aggregations.\\n\\n**Data Structure Layer (pandas-dev/pandas)**: pandas-dev/pandas extends NumPy by wrapping raw arrays through the NDArrayBackedExtensionArray class in pandas/core/arrays/_mixins.py. This class inherits from both NDArrayBacked (a Cython base class) and ExtensionArray (the pandas extension array interface), storing the actual NumPy ndarray in the _ndarray attribute. This architecture allows pandas to maintain transparency with NumPy\u2014operations on pandas extension arrays backed by NDArrayBackedExtensionArray delegate to the underlying NumPy array, enabling seamless integration. Subclasses like Categorical, DatetimeArray, and TimedeltaArray all build on this foundation.\\n\\n**Scientific Computation Layer (scipy/scipy)**: scipy/scipy consumes arrays from both numpy and pandas through the describe() function in scipy/stats/_stats_py.py. The describe() function accepts array_like inputs (supporting both raw NumPy arrays and pandas Series), validates them using array_namespace protocols, and then applies multiple statistical operations: min/max via xp.min() and xp.max(), central tendency via xp.mean(), dispersion via _var(), and shape measures via skew() and kurtosis(). The function returns a DescribeResult namedtuple containing comprehensive summary statistics.\\n\\n**Integration Pattern**: A user starting with raw data flows through this stack as follows: (1) create a NumPy array using standard creation functions, (2) optionally wrap it in a pandas Series/DataFrame using NDArrayBackedExtensionArray for labeled access and convenience methods, (3) pass the array or Series to scipy.stats.describe() which internally extracts the NumPy array and applies statistical transformations. This layered design maintains clear separation of concerns\u2014numpy handles computation, pandas provides data structures, and scipy applies domain-specific statistical analysis\u2014while preserving performance through direct array access at each level.\"\n}\n",
